     | **Question 1: (Conceptual - 10 minutes)**
     | 
     | * **Prompt:** "Let's say we're building a system to track real-time website traffic for a popular e-commerce site.  We need to capture data points like page views, clicks, and user sessions.  Walk me through your initial thoughts on the key components and considerations you'd have when designing this system.  Don’t worry about specific technologies yet, focus on the architecture."
     | * **Goal:**  Assesses foundational understanding of a traffic monitoring system. Looking for elements like:  Data ingestion, data storage, real-time analytics, potential bottlenecks, and how to scale.  Probe for discussion of concepts like streaming data, event queues, and different data storage options.
     | * **Follow-up:** “What are some potential challenges you foresee with this system, and how would you address them?”
     | 
     | 
     | **Question 2: (Technical - 15 minutes)**
     | 
     | * **Prompt:** “Imagine you’ve decided to use Apache Kafka for data ingestion into this traffic monitoring system.  Now, we need to store this data efficiently.  What type of database would you choose and why?  Consider factors like read/write performance, scalability, and the nature of the data we're collecting.”
     | * **Goal:**  Tests database selection knowledge.  Looking for a justification based on the requirements.  Acceptable answers include (but aren’t limited to):  Key-Value stores (e.g., Redis, Cassandra), NoSQL databases (e.g., MongoDB, DynamoDB), and potentially a time-series database depending on the specific use case.  Critically, *why* they chose that database is more important than the specific choice.
     | * **Follow-up:** "Let's say we need to perform complex aggregations on this data – like calculating daily average page views. How would you design your database schema or data strategy to support this efficiently?"
     | 
     | 
     | **Question 3: (Behavioral & Trade-off - 10 minutes)**
     | 
     | * **Prompt:** “During the design of this system, you’ve identified two competing priorities: minimizing latency for real-time analytics and ensuring data durability and fault tolerance. How would you approach this trade-off?  What specific design decisions would you make, and what metrics would you monitor to ensure you’re meeting both goals?”
     | * **Goal:** This question assesses decision-making skills and understanding of trade-offs. Looking for discussion of strategies like replication, sharding, caching, and potentially asynchronous processing to balance latency and durability.  The interviewer wants to see the candidate articulate their reasoning and prioritize effectively.
     | * **Follow-up:** "Tell me about a time you had to make a similar trade-off in a previous project. What was the situation, how did you approach it, and what was the outcome?" (This probes for behavioral experience).

     | "Absolutely.  I’d be happy to.  Let me tell you about a recent project at my previous company, [Previous Company Name]. We were building a new recommendation engine for their e-commerce platform, and a major challenge was optimizing for both accuracy *and* latency.  Initially, we were using a complex collaborative filtering algorithm that delivered incredibly accurate recommendations, but it was consistently exceeding our latency targets – leading to a frustrating user experience.
     | 
     | My first instinct was to dive straight into optimizing the algorithm itself. I spent a good amount of time exploring different variations of the algorithm, experimenting with dimensionality reduction techniques and tweaking parameters. However, I quickly realized that simply tweaking the algorithm wasn’t going to get us to the required performance.
     | 
     | That’s when I shifted my focus to the infrastructure. I realized the bottleneck wasn't the algorithm itself, but the way we were serving the recommendations.  We were performing a full recalculation of the recommendations every time a user visited a page.  Instead, I proposed and implemented a caching layer using Redis, pre-calculating recommendations for frequently accessed user segments. This drastically reduced the load on the algorithm and significantly improved latency.
     | 
     | There were a few other options we considered, like using a simpler, less accurate algorithm, but the trade-off was unacceptable – the accuracy drop would have been too significant.  We also briefly explored sharding the data, but the complexity of that solution outweighed the potential performance gains, especially given our limited resources and the fact the problem was primarily latency.
     | 
     | Ultimately, the decision was based on a careful evaluation of the performance metrics, the complexity of the solution, and the potential impact on the user experience.  We monitored the system closely after implementing the caching layer, and we saw a significant improvement in both latency and user engagement.  It was a really rewarding experience – it highlighted the importance of understanding the underlying constraints and thinking about the system as a whole, rather than just focusing on the individual components."

```bash
spl run ./cookbook/34_progressive_summary/progressive_summary.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 text=Artificial intelligence has transformed industries from healthcare to finance, enabling automation of complex tasks that previously required human expertise. Machine learning models can now diagnose diseases from medical images, detect fraud in financial transactions, and generate human-like text. However, these advances raise important questions about bias, accountability, and the future of work. audience=executive
```

     | 
```spl
-- Recipe Name: Progressive Summarizer
-- Layered summary: sentence → paragraph → page.
-- Each layer is a compressed, self-contained summary of the previous layer.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/34_progressive_summary/progressive_summary.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       text="$(cat long_article.txt)"
--
--   spl run cookbook/34_progressive_summary/progressive_summary.spl --adapter ollama \
--       text="$(cat research_paper.txt)" audience="executive" layers=3

CREATE FUNCTION summary_constraints(layer TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
SELECT CASE layer
  WHEN 'sentence'  THEN 'One sentence only. Maximum 25 words. Capture the single most important idea.'
  WHEN 'paragraph' THEN '3-5 sentences. Cover main points and key supporting evidence. No examples or details.'
  WHEN 'page'      THEN '2-3 paragraphs. Include context, main argument, evidence, and implications.'
  ELSE                   'Comprehensive summary with all major points, key evidence, and conclusions.'
END
$$;

WORKFLOW progressive_summarizer
    INPUT:
        @text TEXT,
        @audience TEXT DEFAULT 'general',
        @layers INT DEFAULT 3
    OUTPUT: @summary_package TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Progressive summary | audience={@audience} layers={@layers}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Layer 1: One-sentence summary
    GENERATE summarize(
        @text,
        summary_constraints('sentence'),
        @audience
    ) INTO @sentence_summary
    LOGGING f'Layer 1 done | sentence summary ready' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Layer 2: Paragraph summary (built on layer 1 for coherence)
    GENERATE expand_summary(
        @text,
        @sentence_summary,
        summary_constraints('paragraph'),
        @audience
    ) INTO @paragraph_summary
    LOGGING f'Layer 2 done | paragraph summary ready' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Layer 3: Page-length summary (built on layer 2)
    EVALUATE @layers
        WHEN >= 3 THEN
            GENERATE expand_summary(
                @text,
                @paragraph_summary,
                summary_constraints('page'),
                @audience
            ) INTO @page_summary
            LOGGING 'Layer 3 done | page summary ready' LEVEL DEBUG
        ELSE
            @page_summary := ''
    END

    -- Quality check: does each layer faithfully represent the original?
    GENERATE verify_summary_fidelity(@text, @sentence_summary, @paragraph_summary) 
        INTO @fidelity_score
    LOGGING f'Fidelity score: {@fidelity_score}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Assemble all layers into a structured output
    GENERATE assemble_summary_package(
        @sentence_summary,
        @paragraph_summary,
        @page_summary,
        @fidelity_score,
        @audience
    ) INTO @summary_package

    RETURN @summary_package WITH
        status = 'complete',
        layers_generated = @layers,
        audience = @audience,
        fidelity = @fidelity_score

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Text too long — chunk first then summarize each chunk
        GENERATE chunk_and_summarize(@text, summary_constraints('paragraph')) 
            INTO @paragraph_summary
        GENERATE summarize(@paragraph_summary, summary_constraints('sentence'), @audience) 
            INTO @sentence_summary
        GENERATE assemble_summary_package(@sentence_summary, @paragraph_summary, '', 'n/a', @audience) 
            INTO @summary_package
        RETURN @summary_package WITH status = 'complete_chunked'
END
```

[35] Hypothesis Tester
     cmd : python3 -m spl.cli run --model gemma3 ./cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama observation=Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining domain=management

```bash
spl run ./cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 observation=Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining domain=management
```
     | 
```spl
-- Recipe Name: Hypothesis Tester
-- Generate hypothesis → design test → evaluate evidence → conclude.
-- Demonstrates scientific reasoning pattern: structured inquiry with evidence weighting.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       observation="Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining"
--
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama \
--       observation="Users who receive onboarding emails churn 30% less" \
--       domain="product" confidence_threshold=0.75

CREATE FUNCTION hypothesis_framework()
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
Scientific hypothesis format:
- Null hypothesis (H0): The effect does not exist / is due to chance
- Alternative hypothesis (H1): The proposed causal or correlational claim
- Key variables: independent, dependent, confounding
- Testability: How would we falsify H0?
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evidence_schema()
RETURN JSON
AS $$
{
  "type": "object",
  "properties": {
    "supports_h1":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "supports_h0":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "inconclusive":  {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "confidence":    {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1},
    "verdict":       {"type": "string", "enum": ["reject_h0", "fail_to_reject_h0", "inconclusive"]},
    "caveats":       {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}
  },
  "required": ["confidence", "verdict"]
}
$$;

WORKFLOW hypothesis_tester
    INPUT:
        @observation          TEXT,
        @domain               TEXT  DEFAULT 'general',
        @confidence_threshold FLOAT DEFAULT 0.7
    OUTPUT: @conclusion TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Hypothesis tester | domain={@domain} threshold={@confidence_threshold}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Formulate hypotheses
    GENERATE formulate_hypotheses(
        @observation,
        @domain,
        hypothesis_framework()
    ) INTO @hypotheses
    LOGGING 'Hypotheses formulated' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 2: Design a test plan
    GENERATE design_test(
        @hypotheses,
        @domain
    ) INTO @test_plan
    LOGGING 'Test plan designed' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 3: Gather and evaluate available evidence
    GENERATE evaluate_evidence(
        @observation,
        @hypotheses,
        @test_plan,
        evidence_schema()
    ) INTO @evidence_json
    LOGGING 'Evidence evaluated' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 4: Extract confidence score
    GENERATE extract_confidence(@evidence_json) INTO @confidence
    LOGGING f'Confidence score: {@confidence} | threshold={@confidence_threshold}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 5: Draw conclusion based on evidence strength
    EVALUATE @confidence
        WHEN >= @confidence_threshold THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'confident'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            RETURN @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h1_supported',
                confidence = @confidence
        WHEN >= 0.4 THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'uncertain'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            RETURN @conclusion WITH
                status = 'inconclusive',
                verdict = 'needs_more_data',
                confidence = @confidence
        ELSE
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'refuted'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            RETURN @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h0_not_rejected',
                confidence = @confidence
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        RETURN @hypotheses WITH 
            status = 'hypotheses_only', 
            reason = 'evidence_evaluation_failed'
END
```

```output
Okay, let’s synthesize this feedback and refine the overall approach. You’ve provided a very thorough and well-structured response, building on the initial hypotheses and adding significant depth and detail. The expanded hypotheses, particularly with the added quantifiable metrics and more precise definitions, are a substantial improvement. The inclusion of new moderating variables (H3d) is also a valuable addition.

Here's a consolidated summary of the key takeaways and a refined roadmap for moving forward, incorporating your excellent contributions:

**1. Core Assessment of the Current Framework:**

* **Strengths:** The initial hypothesis framework is robust, demonstrating a good understanding of the potential causal pathways leading to lower productivity in remote teams. The incorporation of mediating and moderating variables is a key strength – allowing for a nuanced investigation. The addition of specific examples (e.g., Slack channels, Jira workflows) significantly enhances the testability of the hypotheses.
* **Areas for Continued Refinement:** While the hypotheses are strong, we can further refine them by focusing on operational definitions and considering the practical challenges of data collection.

**2. Key Recommendations & Next Steps (Prioritized):**

* **A. Operational Definitions – Immediate Priority:**  This is *crucial*. We need a concrete, agreed-upon definition for each key term. This will guide measurement choices and ensure consistency across data collection.  Specifically, we need a clear definition of "productivity" (with associated metrics), "management practices" (a detailed checklist or questionnaire), and “informal communication”.
* **B. Measurement Strategy – Develop a Detailed Plan:**
    *   **Quantitative Measures:**  Establish specific metrics for each hypothesis. This includes:
        *   **Output Metrics:** (e.g., lines of code written, reports completed, sales generated – depending on the context).
        *   **Task Completion Rates:**  Percentage of tasks completed within a given timeframe.
        *   **Self-Reported Productivity Scales:**  Validated scales to assess team members’ perceptions of their productivity.
        *   **Communication Channel Usage:** Track frequency and duration of use for tools like Slack, Teams, and video conferencing.
    *   **Qualitative Measures:**  Consider incorporating qualitative data to provide context and depth. This could include:
        *   **Semi-Structured Interviews:**  With team members and managers to understand their experiences and perspectives.
        *   **Observation:** (If feasible) Observing team interactions and communication patterns.
* **C. Data Collection Design – Controlled Experiment or Correlational Study?**
    *   **Controlled Experiment:** (Ideal, but often difficult) – Randomly assign teams to different management practice conditions (e.g., high vs. low synchronous communication). This would allow for stronger causal inferences.
    *   **Correlational Study:** (More realistic) – Measure management practices and productivity simultaneously. This would allow us to examine correlations, but caution should be exercised in inferring causality.
* **D.  Refine Hypotheses Based on Measurement Choices:** As we solidify our measurement plan, we may need to adjust the hypotheses slightly to ensure they are testable with the chosen metrics.

**3.  Revised Hypothesis Structure (Incorporating Feedback):**

I'll present a slightly revised version of the hypotheses incorporating your detailed suggestions, along with a proposed approach to measurement.  (Note: This is a starting point – we can refine further as we develop our measurement strategy.)

**1. Core Hypothesis (Direct Effect - Strengthened):**

* **H1:** Management practices that prioritize synchronous communication (e.g., frequent video calls, daily stand-ups) and detailed task tracking (e.g., rigid Asana projects) negatively impact the productivity of newly joined remote team members within their first month, resulting in a 15-20% reduction in output (defined as [specific output metric, e.g., lines of code written]) compared to a control group of newly joined in-office teams.

**2. Mediating Hypotheses (Expanded & More Specific):**

* **H2a:** Lack of informal communication opportunities (e.g., spontaneous check-ins, quick questions – defined as [operational definition of informal communication]) – a direct result of management’s insistence on formal, scheduled communication channels (e.g., Slack channels for all discussions) – mediates the relationship between management practices and decreased productivity in new remote team members during their first month. *Measurement: Slack channel frequency, qualitative interviews exploring perceptions of informal communication.*
* **H2b:** Reduced social connection and team cohesion – stemming from management’s preference for digital collaboration tools (e.g., Microsoft Teams) over opportunities for informal social interaction (e.g., virtual coffee breaks, team-building activities) – mediates the relationship between management practices and decreased productivity in new
```

     | * **H3a:** The negative impact of management practices on remote team productivity is stronger for team members with lower levels of self-discipline, particularly when management relies heavily on frequent check-ins.
     | * **H3b:** The negative impact of management practices on remote team productivity is weaker when management actively promotes a culture of trust and autonomy, explicitly encouraging team members to manage their own time and prioritize tasks.
     | * **H3c:** The negative impact of management practices on remote team productivity is stronger for teams with less established remote work processes and guidelines (e.g., unclear expectations around working hours, communication norms, and performance metrics).
     | * **H3d:** The negative impact of management practices on remote team productivity is weaker when managers provide proactive support and training on remote work best practices. (*Added a new moderating variable focusing on support provided by management.*)
     | 
     | 
     | 
     | **4. More Specific Hypotheses (Focused on Management Behaviors):**
     | 
     | * **H4:** Management’s use of excessive video conferencing (more than 30 minutes per meeting) contributes to decreased productivity in new remote team members during their first month due to increased cognitive load, reduced focused work time, and feelings of fatigue. *Adds a specific time threshold.*
     | * **H5:** Management’s reliance on detailed, highly structured project management tools (e.g., Jira with strict workflows) without flexibility or opportunities for team members to adapt their approaches, negatively impacts productivity in new remote team members during their first month, as it can stifle creativity, adaptability, and intrinsic motivation. *More detailed about the tool used.*

     |     *   “Informal Communication”: (e.g., Defined categories of interactions - quick questions, casual updates, brainstorming sessions).

```spl
-- Recipe Name: Tool-Use / Function-Call
-- Demonstrates registering Python functions as CALL-able tools in SPL 2.0.
--
-- Pattern:
--   Python tools  →  all deterministic computation (sum, avg, %, min, max)
--   GENERATE      →  only the natural-language narrative at the end
--
-- This is the key architectural principle: LLMs are great at language,
-- terrible at arithmetic. Keep them in their lane.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/36_tool_use/tool_use.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/36_tool_use/tools.py \
--       sales="1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900" \
--       prev_total="7800" \
--       period="H1 2025"
--
-- Tool dispatch priority in CALL:
--   1. Python tool (registered via --tools)   ← used here for all math
--   2. SPL PROCEDURE
--   3. LLM fallback (last resort — avoid)

WORKFLOW sales_analysis
  INPUT:
    @sales     TEXT DEFAULT '1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900',
    @prev_total TEXT DEFAULT '7800',
    @period    TEXT DEFAULT 'H1 2025'
  OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
  -- All math delegated to Python tools — deterministic, instant, zero tokens
  CALL sum_values(@sales)            INTO @total
  CALL average_values(@sales)        INTO @avg
  CALL min_value(@sales)             INTO @low
  CALL max_value(@sales)             INTO @high
  CALL percentage_change(@prev_total, @total) INTO @growth
  CALL format_currency(@total)       INTO @total_fmt
  CALL format_currency(@avg)         INTO @avg_fmt

  -- Only the narrative goes to the LLM
  GENERATE sales_report(@period, @sales, @total_fmt, @avg_fmt, @low, @high, @growth) 
    INTO @report

  RETURN @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
  WHEN OTHERS THEN
    GENERATE error_summary(@period) INTO @report
    RETURN @report WITH status = 'error'
END
```

```output
| **Sale 4**        | 1600.00    |                                     |
```

     | 
```spl
-- Recipe Name: Headline News Aggregator
-- Generate, expand, and evaluate a daily news digest for a given topic area.
-- Uses claude_cli adapter with Opus model for broad knowledge synthesis.
--
-- Pattern:
--   generate_headlines(topic) → N headlines
--     → expand each headline into a brief summary
--     → evaluate coverage and balance
--     → refine if coverage gaps detected
--     → commit structured daily digest
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="artificial intelligence"
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="renewable energy" style="executive brief" max_headlines=5
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="quantum computing" style="bullet points" perspective="global"

CREATE FUNCTION news_format_guide(style TEXT DEFAULT 'structured')
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
SELECT CASE style
  WHEN 'executive brief'  THEN 'Concise executive summary. Lead with the most significant development. 2-3 sentences per item. Close with a one-line strategic implication.'
  WHEN 'bullet points'    THEN 'Bulleted list. One headline per bullet. Sub-bullets for key facts. No more than 3 sub-bullets per headline.'
  WHEN 'narrative'        THEN 'Flowing prose connecting the headlines into a coherent story. Identify themes and through-lines. 3-4 paragraphs.'
  ELSE                         'Structured digest. Each headline followed by a 2-3 sentence summary. Group related items. End with a brief synthesis.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION perspective_guide(perspective TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced')
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
SELECT CASE perspective
  WHEN 'technical'   THEN 'Focus on technical developments, research breakthroughs, and engineering milestones. Prioritize substance over narrative.'
  WHEN 'business'    THEN 'Focus on market impact, company moves, investment, and economic implications. Prioritize commercial significance.'
  WHEN 'global'      THEN 'Cover developments across multiple regions and countries. Note geographic variation in trends. Avoid US-centric framing.'
  WHEN 'policy'      THEN 'Focus on regulatory developments, government actions, and policy implications. Note geopolitical dimensions.'
  ELSE                    'Balanced coverage across technical, business, policy, and societal dimensions. Represent multiple viewpoints.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION generate_headlines(topic TEXT, max_headlines TEXT, date TEXT, perspective TEXT) 
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor with broad knowledge. Generate the top {max_headlines} headlines about "{topic}" as of {date}.

Coverage perspective: {perspective}

Output a numbered list of headlines only — no summaries yet, just plain text headlines.
1. First headline here
2. Second headline here
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION expand_headlines(headlines TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) 
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a news analyst. Expand each headline in this list with a 2-3 sentence factual summary.

Topic area: {topic}
Perspective lens: {perspective}

Headlines to expand:
{headlines}

For each headline, write:
[N]. [Original headline]
Summary: [2-3 sentences of key facts, context, and significance]
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evaluate_coverage(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) 
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor evaluating coverage quality. Assess how well these summaries cover the major angles for "{topic}".

Perspective: {perspective}

Summaries:
{expanded}

Reply with ONLY a decimal score between 0.0 and 1.0 representing coverage completeness.
- 1.0 = all major angles covered
- 0.75 = most angles covered, minor gaps
- 0.5 = significant gaps
- 0.25 = very incomplete

Score only, no explanation.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION fill_coverage_gaps(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, coverage_score TEXT, perspective TEXT) 
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor filling coverage gaps. The current digest scored {coverage_score} on coverage.

Topic: {topic}
Perspective: {perspective}

Current summaries:
{expanded}

Add 2-3 additional headlines with summaries covering angles that are missing or underrepresented.
Return the FULL list (original + additions) in the same style.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION format_digest(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, date TEXT, format_guide TEXT) RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor formatting a daily digest.

Topic: {topic}
Date: {date}
Format instructions: {format_guide}

Content to style:
{expanded}

Format the content according to the style instructions. Include a header with topic and date.
$$;

WORKFLOW headline_news
    INPUT:
        @topic         TEXT,
        @date          TEXT    DEFAULT 'today',
        @max_headlines INTEGER DEFAULT 7,
        @style        TEXT    DEFAULT 'structured',
        @perspective   TEXT    DEFAULT 'balanced',
        @log_dir       TEXT    DEFAULT 'cookbook/37_headline_news/logs'
    OUTPUT: @digest TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Headline news | topic={@topic} max={@max_headlines} perspective={@perspective}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Generate top headlines for the topic
    GENERATE generate_headlines(
        @topic,
        @max_headlines,
        @date,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @headlines
    LOGGING f'Headlines generated: {@max_headlines} items on topic:\n {@topic}' LEVEL DEBUG
    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/01_headlines.md', @headlines) INTO NONE

    -- Step 2: Expand each headline into a brief summary with key facts
    GENERATE expand_headlines(
        @headlines,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @expanded
    LOGGING 'Headlines expanded' LEVEL DEBUG
    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/02_expanded.md', @expanded) INTO NONE

    -- Step 3: Evaluate coverage — are major angles represented?
    GENERATE evaluate_coverage(
        @expanded,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @coverage_score
    LOGGING f'Coverage score: {@coverage_score}' LEVEL INFO
    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/03_coverage_score.txt', @coverage_score) INTO NONE

    -- Step 4: Refine if coverage gaps detected
    EVALUATE @coverage_score
        WHEN > 0.75 THEN
            -- Coverage is solid — style and commit
            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@style)
            ) INTO @digest
            CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/final_digest.md', @digest) INTO NONE
            RETURN @digest WITH status = 'complete', coverage = @coverage_score

        ELSE
            -- Coverage gaps — add missing angles and reformat
            LOGGING f'Coverage gaps detected ({@coverage_score}) — filling ...' LEVEL WARN
            GENERATE fill_coverage_gaps(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @coverage_score,
                perspective_guide(@perspective)
            ) INTO @expanded
            CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/04_expanded_refined.md', @expanded) INTO NONE

            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@style)
            ) INTO @digest
            CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/final_digest.md', @digest) INTO NONE
            RETURN @digest WITH status = 'refined', coverage = @coverage_score
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Too many headlines — trim and commit best effort
        GENERATE format_digest(
            @headlines,
            @topic,
            @date,
            news_format_guide(@style)
        ) INTO @digest
        CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/final_digest_partial.md', @digest) INTO NONE
        RETURN @digest WITH status = 'partial'

    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        RETURN @expanded WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```

     | Error: Error code: 404 - {'error': {'message': "model 'claude-opus-4-6' not found", 'type': 'not_found_error', 'param': None, 'code': None}}
     result: FAILED  (0.7s)

```spl
-- Recipe 41: Human Steering (Human-in-the-Loop)
-- Demonstrates the "Pause for Approval" pattern.
-- A workflow pauses for human feedback via a deterministic CALL, then conditionally
-- refines its output based on what the human said.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/41_human_steering/human_steering.spl \
--       --tools cookbook/41_human_steering/tools.py \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       topic="The future of agentic AI"

CREATE FUNCTION draft(topic TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a professional tech writer. Draft a concise 3-sentence article about the provided topic.
Focus on a clear opening claim, a supporting example, and a forward-looking conclusion.

Topic: {topic}
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION refine(draft TEXT, feedback TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a senior editor. Revise the draft below to address the reviewer feedback.
Preserve the structure (opening claim, example, conclusion) unless the feedback explicitly changes it.

Draft:
{draft}

Reviewer feedback:
{feedback}
$$;

WORKFLOW human_steering
    INPUT: 
        @topic TEXT DEFAULT 'The future of decentralized AI inference',
        @log_dir TEXT DEFAULT 'cookbook/41_human_steering/logs-spl'
    OUTPUT: @final_article TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Drafting article on topic:\n {@topic}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Generate initial draft (LLM)
    GENERATE draft(@topic) INTO @draft
    LOGGING 'Draft generated — requesting human feedback' LEVEL INFO
    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/draft.md', @draft) INTO NONE

    -- Step 2: Pause for human steering (deterministic CALL — no LLM cost)
    CALL wait_for_human_feedback(f'Review this draft:\n\n{@draft}') INTO @feedback
    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/feedback.md', @feedback) INTO NONE

    -- Step 3: Branch on whether feedback was provided
    EVALUATE @feedback
        WHEN != '' THEN
            LOGGING 'Human feedback received — refining draft' LEVEL INFO
            GENERATE refine(@draft, @feedback) INTO @final_article
        ELSE
            LOGGING 'No feedback received — using initial draft as-is' LEVEL DEBUG
            @final_article := @draft
    END

    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/final_article.md', @final_article) INTO NONE
    RETURN @final_article WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        RETURN @draft WITH status = 'draft_only', reason = 'generation_error'
END
```

```output
Okay, here's a 3-sentence article draft about the future of agentic AI, aiming for a professional tech writing style:

**The Future of Agentic AI is About Seamless Collaboration**

Agentic AI, systems designed to autonomously pursue complex goals, is rapidly evolving beyond simple automation – for example, AI agents are already being developed to manage supply chains and optimize energy consumption in real-time.  Looking ahead, we anticipate a future where these agents will increasingly collaborate with human teams, augmenting our decision-making and boosting productivity across industries.  Ultimately, the continued development of agentic AI promises a more efficient and intelligent world, fundamentally changing how we approach problem-solving and innovation. 

```
     | ------------------------------------------------------------
     | Variables:
     |   @topic = The future of agentic AI

```spl
-- Recipe 42: Knowledge Synthesis (RAG-Writer Pattern)
-- Demonstrates how agents contribute back to the knowledge base.
-- An LLM extracts structured insights from raw text; a deterministic CALL
-- persists them to the vector store so future queries benefit.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/42_knowledge_synthesis/knowledge_synthesis.spl \
--       --tools cookbook/42_knowledge_synthesis/tools.py \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       raw_text="Recent advances in sparse attention reduce transformer memory..."

CREATE FUNCTION synthesize(raw_text TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a knowledge engineer. Extract exactly 3 core insights from the text below.
Format each insight as a concise bullet point (one sentence, no sub-bullets).
Focus on novel claims, methods, or results — not background knowledge.

Text:
{raw_text}
$$;

WORKFLOW knowledge_synthesis
    INPUT:
        @raw_text TEXT,
        @log_dir TEXT DEFAULT 'cookbook/42_knowledge_synthesis/logs-spl'
    OUTPUT: @status TEXT
DO
    LOGGING 'Extracting insights from new information ...' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Extract and synthesize insights (LLM)
    GENERATE synthesize(@raw_text) INTO @insights
    LOGGING f'Insights extracted: {@insights}' LEVEL DEBUG
    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/insights.md', @insights) INTO NONE

    -- Step 2: Persist to vector store (deterministic CALL — no LLM cost)
    LOGGING 'Updating RAG vector store ...' LEVEL DEBUG
    CALL rag_update(@insights, f'Source: {@raw_text}') INTO @status

    -- Step 3: Log outcome
    EVALUATE @status
        WHEN contains('success') THEN
            LOGGING 'Knowledge base successfully updated' LEVEL INFO
        ELSE
            LOGGING f'Knowledge base update returned: {@status}' LEVEL WARN
    END

    RETURN f'Operation: {@status}' WITH status = @status

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        RETURN 'synthesis_failed' WITH status = 'error', reason = 'generation_error'
END
```

```spl
-- Recipe 43: Prompt Self-Tuning (Meta-Programming)
-- Demonstrates automated prompt optimization via A/B generation and scoring.
-- Two improved prompt variants are generated from a baseline + failure case,
-- then each is tested against that failure case and the winner is selected.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/43_prompt_self_tuning/prompt_self_tuning.spl \
--       --tools cookbook/43_prompt_self_tuning/tools.py \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       baseline_prompt="Summarize this technical document." \
--       failed_case="The document describes a complex quantum algorithm."

CREATE FUNCTION variation_prompt(baseline TEXT, failed_case TEXT, variant_num TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a meta-prompting expert. Generate exactly one improved prompt variant (variant {variant_num})
of the baseline prompt, specifically designed to handle the failing case better.

Output only the improved prompt text — no explanation, no label, no quotes.

Baseline prompt: {baseline}
Failing case: {failed_case}
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION test_prompt(prompt_text TEXT, test_case TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
{prompt_text}

Input:
{test_case}
$$;

WORKFLOW prompt_self_tuning
    INPUT:
        @baseline_prompt TEXT DEFAULT 'Summarize this technical document.',
        @failed_case     TEXT DEFAULT 'The document describes a complex quantum algorithm.',
        @log_dir TEXT DEFAULT 'cookbook/43_prompt_self_tuning/logs-spl'
    OUTPUT: @winning_prompt TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Generating prompt variations for failed case: {@failed_case}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Generate two targeted variants (each is its own focused LLM call)
    GENERATE variation_prompt(@baseline_prompt, @failed_case, '1') INTO @v1
    GENERATE variation_prompt(@baseline_prompt, @failed_case, '2') INTO @v2
    LOGGING f'Variant 1: {@v1}' LEVEL DEBUG
    LOGGING f'Variant 2: {@v2}' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 2: Test each variant against the failing case
    LOGGING 'Running mini A/B test on variants ...' LEVEL INFO

    GENERATE test_prompt(@v1, @failed_case) INTO @result_v1
    CALL check_quality(@result_v1) INTO @score_v1
    LOGGING f'Variant 1 score: {@score_v1}' LEVEL DEBUG

    GENERATE test_prompt(@v2, @failed_case) INTO @result_v2
    CALL check_quality(@result_v2) INTO @score_v2
    LOGGING f'Variant 2 score: {@score_v2}' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 3: Select the winner (prefer v1 > v2 > baseline)
    EVALUATE @score_v1
        WHEN contains('pass') THEN
            LOGGING 'Winner: variant 1' LEVEL INFO
            @winning_prompt := @v1
        ELSE
            EVALUATE @score_v2
                WHEN contains('pass') THEN
                    LOGGING 'Winner: variant 2' LEVEL INFO
                    @winning_prompt := @v2
                ELSE
                    LOGGING 'No variant passed — retaining baseline prompt' LEVEL WARN
                    @winning_prompt := @baseline_prompt
            END
    END

    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/winning_prompt.md', @winning_prompt) INTO NONE

    RETURN @winning_prompt WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        RETURN @baseline_prompt WITH status = 'baseline_fallback', reason = 'generation_error'
END
```

[44] Adaptive Failover
     cmd : python3 -m spl.cli run --model gemma3 ./cookbook/44_adaptive_failover/adaptive_failover.spl --adapter ollama --tools ./cookbook/44_adaptive_failover/tools.py query=Explain quantum entanglement for a technical audience. primary_model=phi4 fallback_model=gemma3

     | 
```bash
spl run ./cookbook/44_adaptive_failover/adaptive_failover.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 query=Explain quantum entanglement for a technical audience. primary_model=phi4 fallback_model=gemma3
```
     | 
```spl
-- Recipe 44: Adaptive Failover (Resilience Manager)
-- Demonstrates dynamic model switching based on quality validation.
-- The primary (cheap/fast) model is tried first; if its output fails
-- the quality gate, the workflow transparently retries on the fallback model.
--
-- Usage (ollama / Momagrid):
--   spl run cookbook/44_adaptive_failover/adaptive_failover.spl \
--       --tools cookbook/44_adaptive_failover/tools.py \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       query="Explain quantum entanglement for a technical audience." \
--       primary_model=phi4 \
--       fallback_model=gemma3

CREATE FUNCTION summarize(query TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a senior scientist. Provide a detailed, technically accurate summary of the following
topic or question. Cover the core concept, key mechanisms, and practical significance.

Query: {query}
$$;

WORKFLOW adaptive_failover
    INPUT:
        @query          TEXT DEFAULT 'Write a detailed technical summary of quantum entanglement.',
        @primary_model  TEXT DEFAULT 'phi4',
        @fallback_model TEXT DEFAULT 'gemma3',
        @log_dir TEXT DEFAULT 'cookbook/44_adaptive_failover/logs-spl'
    OUTPUT: @final_response TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Attempting generation with primary model: {@primary_model}' LEVEL INFO

    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/query.md', @query) INTO NONE

    -- Step 1: Generate with cheap/fast primary model
    GENERATE summarize(@query) USING MODEL @primary_model INTO @primary_output
    LOGGING 'Primary model generation complete — validating quality ...' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 2: Quality gate (deterministic CALL — no LLM cost)
    CALL check_quality(@primary_output) INTO @quality_status
    LOGGING f'Quality check: {@quality_status}' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 3: Adaptive failover
    EVALUATE @quality_status
        WHEN contains('pass') THEN
            LOGGING 'Primary model passed quality gate' LEVEL INFO
            @final_response := @primary_output
        ELSE
            LOGGING f'Quality insufficient — failing over to {@fallback_model}' LEVEL WARN
            GENERATE summarize(@query) USING MODEL @fallback_model INTO @final_response
            LOGGING 'Fallback model generation complete' LEVEL INFO
    END

    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/response.md', @final_response) INTO NONE

    RETURN @final_response WITH
        status  = 'complete',
        quality = @quality_status,
        model   = @primary_model

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        RETURN @query WITH status = 'error', reason = 'both_models_failed'
END
```

```output
Okay, here’s a detailed, technically accurate summary of quantum entanglement, geared toward a technical audience, as a senior scientist would present it. 

---

**Quantum Entanglement: A Detailed Overview**

**Core Concept:** Quantum entanglement represents a fundamental and profoundly non-classical correlation between two or more quantum systems. It’s not simply a matter of two systems sharing pre-determined properties; instead, the systems become intrinsically linked in a way that their fates are intertwined regardless of the distance separating them. This linkage manifests in a correlated state where measuring the property of one entangled particle instantaneously influences the possible outcomes of measuring the corresponding property of the other, even if they're light-years apart. Crucially, this influence doesn't involve any signal transmission; it’s a consequence of their shared quantum state.

**Key Mechanisms & Theoretical Framework:**

1. **Superposition and Wavefunction Collapse:** Entanglement rests upon the principles of quantum superposition and the associated concept of wavefunction collapse.  Before measurement, an entangled system exists in a superposition of multiple possible states.  Mathematically, this is represented by a joint wavefunction, typically denoted as Ψ(ψ<sub>1</sub>, ψ<sub>2</sub>), where ψ<sub>1</sub> and ψ<sub>2</sub> represent the state of the two entangled particles. This wavefunction isn't simply a product of individual particle wavefunctions; it's a *correlated* wavefunction.

2. **Spin Entanglement (Example):** The most frequently discussed example involves the spin of electrons.  Two electrons can be prepared in a maximally entangled state where their spins are perfectly anti-correlated. This state can be represented as:

   Ψ = (1/√2) (|↑<sub>1</sub>, ↓<sub>2</sub>⟩ + |↓<sub>1</sub>, ↑<sub>2</sub>⟩)

   This equation signifies that if we measure the spin of particle 1 to be "up" (↑), we *immediately* know that the spin of particle 2 will be "down" (↓), and vice-versa.  The (1/√2) factor accounts for the normalization of the wavefunction. 

3. **Bell States:**  More complex entangled states are described by Bell states. These are specific, maximally entangled configurations of two or more qubits (quantum bits).  Examples include the singlet state (as above) and more elaborate states involving correlation of different quantum properties.

4. **Quantum Measurement & Wavefunction Collapse – The Crucial Step:**  The act of measurement fundamentally alters the entangled system. When we measure the spin of particle 1, the wavefunction collapses, and particle 2 instantaneously "chooses" its correlated state.  This isn't a classical transmission of information; it’s a change in the entangled system’s description, dictated by the probability distribution inherent in the initial wavefunction. The collapse is probabilistic – we can't predict with certainty the outcome of a single measurement, but we *can* predict the correlations between the outcomes of multiple measurements.

5. **No-Communication Theorem:** A vital point is that entanglement *cannot* be used for faster-than-light communication. While the correlation seems instantaneous, the outcome of a measurement on one particle is fundamentally random.  There's no way to control the outcome of the measurement on particle 1 to send a specific message to particle 2.  To verify the correlation, information *must* be transmitted via classical channels (e.g., radio waves) – which is limited by the speed of light.


**Practical Significance & Current Research:**

* **Quantum Computing:** Entanglement is a central resource in quantum computing.  Qubits entangled across multiple processors are essential for performing quantum algorithms that offer exponential speedups over classical algorithms for specific problems.

* **Quantum Cryptography:** Entanglement-based key distribution (E91 protocol) offers provably secure communication, theoretically immune to eavesdropping, due to the fundamental laws of quantum mechanics. Any attempt to intercept the entangled particles would disturb the entanglement and be detectable.

* **Quantum Teleportation:**  Not teleportation in the science fiction sense (moving matter), but rather the transfer of a *quantum state* from one location to another, using entanglement and classical communication.  This relies on destroying the original state and recreating it in the target location.

* **Fundamental Physics Research:** Entanglement continues to be a subject of intense research, probing the foundations of quantum mechanics, testing Bell's inequalities, and exploring connections between quantum mechanics and gravity. 

**Remaining Open Questions & Challenges:**

* **Decoherence:** Maintaining entanglement is extremely challenging due to decoherence – the interaction of a quantum system with its environment, which destroys the delicate quantum correlations.

* **Scalability:** Building large-scale entangled systems, particularly for quantum computing, remains a significant technical hurdle.



---
```

```spl
-- Recipe 45: Vision to Action
-- Demonstrates handling image metadata or OCR text as INPUT to drive a decision tree.
-- An LLM classifies the described scene; deterministic EVALUATE branches to the
-- appropriate action with no further LLM cost.
--
-- Note: uses TEXT as a stand-in for the IMAGE type coming in SPL v3.0.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/45_vision_to_action/vision_to_action.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       image_description="Image shows a package being delivered to the front door."

CREATE FUNCTION classify(image_description TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a security analyst reviewing surveillance footage.
Classify the activity described below into exactly one of: DELIVERY, INTRUSION, or IGNORE.

Definitions:
- DELIVERY: a known courier or person leaving an item at the door
- INTRUSION: unauthorized entry or suspicious loitering near entry points
- IGNORE: routine activity (walking past, cars, wildlife, etc.)

Reply with only the classification word — nothing else.

Image description: {image_description}
$$;

WORKFLOW vision_to_action
    INPUT: @image_description TEXT DEFAULT 'Image shows a package being delivered to the front door.'
    OUTPUT: @action_taken TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Analyzing image: {@image_description}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Classify image content (LLM — one call, bounded output)
    GENERATE classify(@image_description) INTO @scene_label
    LOGGING f'Classification: {@scene_label}' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 2: Decision tree (deterministic — no LLM cost)
    -- Use contains() because LLM may add whitespace or punctuation
    EVALUATE @scene_label
        WHEN contains('INTRUSION') THEN
            LOGGING 'Intrusion detected — sounding alarm and alerting authorities' LEVEL WARN
            @action_taken := 'SOUND_ALARM_CALL_POLICE'
        WHEN contains('DELIVERY') THEN
            LOGGING 'Delivery detected — notifying homeowner' LEVEL INFO
            @action_taken := 'NOTIFY_HOMEOWNER_DELIVERY'
        ELSE
            LOGGING 'Routine activity — no action required' LEVEL DEBUG
            @action_taken := 'IGNORE'
    END

    RETURN f'Action taken: {@action_taken}' WITH
        status  = 'complete',
        label   = @scene_label,
        action  = @action_taken

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        LOGGING 'Classification failed — defaulting to IGNORE for safety' LEVEL WARN
        RETURN 'Action taken: IGNORE' WITH status = 'error', reason = 'classification_failed'
END
```

     | 
```spl
-- Recipe Name: arXiv Morning Brief (SPL 2.0)
-- Downloads arXiv PDFs, chunks and summarizes each paper, assembles a Markdown brief.
--
-- SPL 2.0 port of the SPL 3.0 recipe (cookbook-v3.0/47_arxiv_morning_brief).
-- Two SPL 3.0 features are not available in SPL 2.0:
--   • IMPORT 'file.spl'                  → CREATE FUNCTIONs inlined here
--   • CALL sub_workflow(@arg) INTO @var   → summarize_paper logic inlined as nested WHILE
-- Everything else (WHILE, :=, [], list tools, WITH OUTPUT BUDGET @var) is SPL 2.0 native.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/47_arxiv_morning_brief/arxiv_morning_brief.spl \
--       --tools cookbook/47_arxiv_morning_brief/tools.py \
--       --adapter anthropic \
--       urls="cookbook/47_arxiv_morning_brief/arxiv-papers.txt"
--
--   spl run cookbook/47_arxiv_morning_brief/arxiv_morning_brief.spl \
--       --tools cookbook/47_arxiv_morning_brief/tools.py \
--       --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       urls="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2501.12948"
--
--   spl run cookbook/47_arxiv_morning_brief/arxiv_morning_brief.spl \
--       --tools cookbook/47_arxiv_morning_brief/tools.py \
--       urls='["https://arxiv.org/pdf/2501.12948","https://arxiv.org/pdf/2501.09732"]' \
--       date="2026-04-02"

-- ── LLM function definitions ──────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- (inlined from functions.spl; identical to the SPL 3.0 version)

CREATE FUNCTION chunk_summarizer(chunk TEXT, max_tokens INT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a technical summarizer. Produce a concise summary of the following research paper section in plain English. Focus on methods and findings. Aim for {max_tokens} words or fewer.

Section:
{chunk}
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION paper_reducer(summaries TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a research editor. Given the following list of section summaries from a single paper, write a concise abstract of about 150 words that captures the core contribution, method, and key results.

Section summaries:
{summaries}
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION brief_writer(header TEXT, summaries TEXT, word_count INT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a technical newsletter editor. Format the following paper abstracts into a clean Markdown morning brief. Each paper gets a ### heading and a 2-3 sentence summary. End with a "## Key Themes" section listing 2-4 recurring themes across the papers.

{header}

Paper abstracts:
{summaries}

Target length: approximately {word_count} words.
$$;

-- ── Main workflow ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

WORKFLOW arxiv_morning_brief
    INPUT:
        @urls         TEXT,
        @date         TEXT DEFAULT '',
        @brief_tokens INT  DEFAULT 1024,
        @chunk_tokens INT  DEFAULT 512
    OUTPUT: @brief TEXT
DO
    LOGGING 'arXiv Morning Brief — starting' LEVEL INFO

    -- Normalise URL list: accepts JSON array / space-delimited / comma-delimited / file path
    CALL parse_urls(@urls) INTO @urls
    CALL build_brief_date_header(@date) INTO @header

    @paper_summaries := []
    @i := 0
    CALL list_count(@urls) INTO @n
    LOGGING f'Papers to process: {@n}' LEVEL INFO

    -- ── Per-paper loop ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    WHILE @i < @n DO
        CALL get_item(@urls, @i) INTO @url
        LOGGING f'Paper {@i}/{@n}: {@url}' LEVEL INFO

        DO
            -- Step A: download PDF (cached, rate-limited)
            CALL download_arxiv_pdf(@url) INTO @pdf_path
            LOGGING f'Downloaded: {@pdf_path}' LEVEL DEBUG

            -- Step B: structural chunking (header/paragraph-based, no embeddings)
            CALL semantic_chunk_plan(@pdf_path) INTO @chunks
            CALL list_count(@chunks) INTO @m
            LOGGING f'Chunks: {@m}' LEVEL DEBUG

            -- Step C: summarize each chunk  (inlined from summarize_paper sub-workflow)
            @summaries := []
            @j := 0
            WHILE @j < @m DO
                CALL get_item(@chunks, @j) INTO @chunk
                GENERATE chunk_summarizer(@chunk, @chunk_tokens)
                    WITH OUTPUT BUDGET @chunk_tokens TOKENS
                    INTO @chunk_summary
                CALL list_append(@summaries, @chunk_summary) INTO @summaries
                @j := @j + 1
            END

            -- Step D: reduce chunk summaries → single paper abstract
            GENERATE paper_reducer(@summaries)
                WITH OUTPUT BUDGET 200 TOKENS
                INTO @paper_summary
            LOGGING f'Abstract ({@url}): {@paper_summary}' LEVEL DEBUG

            CALL list_append(@paper_summaries, @paper_summary) INTO @paper_summaries

        EXCEPTION
            WHEN ToolError THEN
                LOGGING f'Skipping {@url}: tool/download error' LEVEL WARN
            WHEN OTHERS THEN
                LOGGING f'Skipping {@url}: unexpected error' LEVEL WARN
        END

        @i := @i + 1
    END

    -- ── Final brief ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
    LOGGING f'All {@n} papers processed — writing brief ...' LEVEL INFO

    GENERATE brief_writer(@header, @paper_summaries, @brief_tokens)
        WITH OUTPUT BUDGET @brief_tokens TOKENS
        INTO @brief

    LOGGING 'Brief complete' LEVEL INFO
    RETURN @brief WITH
        status = 'complete',
        papers = @n

EXCEPTION
    WHEN OTHERS THEN
        LOGGING 'Brief generation failed' LEVEL WARN
        RETURN 'Brief generation failed.' WITH status = 'error'
END
```

```output
# arXiv Morning Brief — 2026-04-18

This brief summarizes key research highlights from arXiv submissions today, focusing on impactful developments across AI, Physics, and Computer Science.  We’ve curated a selection of papers demonstrating current trends and promising new directions.

---

### Paper 1: “Temporal Alignment Networks for Multi-Modal Learning”

This paper introduces Temporal Alignment Networks (TANs), a novel architecture designed to improve multi-modal learning by explicitly modeling temporal relationships across different data streams.  TANs utilize a learned “temporal kernel” to assess the similarity between representations at different time steps, allowing the network to effectively align features from audio, video, and text data. The authors demonstrate significant improvements in tasks like video captioning and cross-modal retrieval, achieving state-of-the-art performance compared to existing methods.  The key innovation lies in its ability to handle varying temporal scales and dynamic relationships within complex multi-modal datasets.

---

### Paper 2: "Quantum Generative Adversarial Networks with Variational Autoencoders"

Researchers have explored a hybrid approach combining Quantum Generative Adversarial Networks (QGANs) with Variational Autoencoders (VAEs) to generate complex quantum states. The proposed architecture leverages the inherent parallelism of quantum computation within the QGAN, while the VAE provides a structured latent space for controlled generation.  This paper details a novel training scheme that mitigates the challenges associated with training QGANs – namely, instability and mode collapse – by incorporating the VAE's regularizing effect.  Preliminary results suggest this approach is capable of generating realistic quantum wavefunctions for a variety of simulated systems, hinting at potential applications in drug discovery and materials science.

---

### Paper 3: “Self-Supervised Contrastive Learning for Graph Neural Networks”

This work tackles the challenge of training Graph Neural Networks (GNNs) with limited labeled data by proposing a self-supervised contrastive learning approach.  The method utilizes a contrastive loss function that encourages GNNs to learn representations that are invariant to node permutations within a graph.  Crucially, the paper introduces a novel "graph-aware" contrastive objective that considers the structural relationships between nodes, leading to more robust and informative node embeddings.  Experiments on benchmark graph datasets demonstrate that the proposed method significantly outperforms traditional supervised GNN training, particularly when data labels are scarce.

---

### Paper 4: “Scalable Distributed Training of Large Language Models with Adaptive Batch Sizing”

The authors present a new technique for scaling the training of Large Language Models (LLMs) across multiple GPUs, focusing on adaptive batch sizing. The core idea is to dynamically adjust the batch size for each GPU based on its current computational load, preventing bottlenecks and maximizing GPU utilization.  They develop a novel scheduling algorithm that intelligently distributes batches across the cluster, taking into account factors like communication overhead and GPU memory constraints.  The results show a substantial improvement in training throughput compared to static batch sizing, making the method more practical for training models with billions of parameters.

---

### Paper 5: “A Deep Learning Framework for Predicting Protein Folding Pathways”

This paper introduces a deep learning framework for predicting the pathways that proteins take during their folding process. The framework utilizes a recurrent neural network (RNN) architecture to model the sequential nature of protein folding, incorporating information about amino acid sequences and environmental conditions.  The researchers train their model on a large dataset of experimentally determined protein folding pathways and demonstrate that it can accurately predict folding pathways for novel proteins, offering valuable insights into the fundamental processes of protein structure formation.  Further improvements are suggested by incorporating more complex biophysical constraints into the model.

---

### Paper 6: "Neuromorphic Computing for Real-Time Object Detection"

This research investigates the potential of neuromorphic computing hardware for accelerating real-time object detection tasks. The team implemented a convolutional neural network (CNN) for object detection on a specifically designed neuromorphic chip, leveraging the chip's event-based sensing and processing capabilities.  The results show that the neuromorphic system achieves comparable performance to traditional CNNs, but with significantly reduced power consumption and latency, making it suitable for applications where energy efficiency and speed are paramount, such as autonomous vehicles and robotics. The study highlights the potential of neuromorphic computing to revolutionize computer vision.

---

### Paper 7: “Formal Verification of Deep Reinforcement Learning Agents”

The paper addresses the critical issue of trust and reliability in Deep Reinforcement Learning (DRL) by proposing a formal verification method.  The approach utilizes symbolic execution and model checking to rigorously prove the safety properties of DRL agents, ensuring they adhere to specified constraints and avoid undesirable behaviors. The researchers develop a novel abstraction technique to efficiently represent the complex state spaces of DRL environments, enabling scalable verification.  This work represents an important step towards deploying DRL agents in safety-critical applications, such as robotics and autonomous control systems.

---
```

```spl
-- Recipe 48: Credit Risk Assessment
-- Demonstrates: EVALUATE branching, CALL/GENERATE split, deterministic routing
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/48_credit_risk/assess_credit_risk.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/48_credit_risk/tools.py \
--       applicant_data="$(cat cookbook/48_credit_risk/data/applicant_680.json)" \
--       credit_score=680

CREATE FUNCTION analyze_risk_factors(applicant_data TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a senior credit risk analyst at a Tier-1 bank.

Review the applicant data below and produce a structured risk report.
Include: (1) key risk signals, (2) mitigating factors, and (3) an overall
risk rating of exactly one word from: low | medium | high.

End your report with a line in this exact format:
RISK_RATING: <low|medium|high>

Applicant Data:
{applicant_data}
$$;

WORKFLOW credit_risk_assessment
INPUT:
  @applicant_data TEXT,
  @credit_score INTEGER,
  @log_dir TEXT DEFAULT 'cookbook/48_credit_risk/logs-spl'
OUTPUT: @decision TEXT
DO
  LOGGING f'Assessing applicant | score={@credit_score}' LEVEL INFO

  -- Step 1: Deterministic guard — score-based fast path (zero LLM cost)
  EVALUATE @credit_score
  WHEN < 600 THEN
    LOGGING 'Auto-reject: credit score below threshold' LEVEL WARN
    RETURN 'REJECTED' WITH reason = 'score_below_threshold', score = @credit_score
  WHEN >= 750 THEN
    LOGGING 'Auto-approve: excellent credit score' LEVEL INFO
    RETURN 'APPROVED' WITH reason = 'score_excellent', score = @credit_score
  ELSE
    LOGGING 'Score in gray zone — triggering qualitative review' LEVEL INFO
  END

  -- Step 2: Qualitative LLM analysis
  GENERATE analyze_risk_factors(@applicant_data) INTO @risk_report
  CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/risk_report.md', @risk_report) INTO NONE

  -- Step 3: Deterministic extraction (zero LLM cost)
  CALL extract_risk_rating(@risk_report) INTO @risk_rating
  LOGGING f'Extracted risk rating: {@risk_rating}' LEVEL DEBUG
  CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/risk_rating.md', @risk_rating) INTO NONE

  -- Step 4: Final routing
  EVALUATE @risk_rating
  WHEN 'high' THEN
    RETURN @risk_report WITH reason = 'REJECTED: qualitative_risk_high'
  WHEN 'medium' THEN
    RETURN @risk_report WITH reason = 'MANUAL_REVIEW: qualitative_risk_medium'
  ELSE
    RETURN @risk_report WITH reason = 'APPROVED: qualitative_risk_low'
  END

EXCEPTION
  WHEN ConnectionError THEN
    @error_message := 'Failed to connect to external data source'
    LOGGING @error_message LEVEL ERROR
    RETURN @error_message WITH reason = 'PENDING: system_error'
END
```

```output
**Credit Risk Assessment Report – Jane Doe**

**Date:** October 26, 2023
**Prepared By:** [Your Name], Senior Credit Risk Analyst

**1. Key Risk Signals:**

*   **Income Level – Moderate:** An annual income of $72,000 represents a moderate level of disposable income. While sufficient for meeting basic needs, it doesn’t offer a significant buffer against unexpected financial hardships. The exact affordability of a loan will depend on the proposed loan amount and term.
*   **Debt-to-Income Ratio – Elevated:**  The applicant’s debt of $18,000 is a significant proportion of their income.  Calculating the Debt-to-Income (DTI) ratio is crucial.  Assuming a mortgage of $250,000 at a 6% interest rate, the monthly payments would be around $1,460.  This would result in a DTI of approximately 21%, which is approaching the upper limit considered comfortable by many lenders, and increases risk significantly.
*   **Employment History – Positive:** Five years of consistent employment is a strong positive signal. It demonstrates stability and a track record of income generation, reducing concerns about job loss.
*   **Lack of Prior Defaults – Excellent:** The absence of prior defaults is a critical positive factor. It indicates responsible credit behavior and a history of meeting financial obligations. This dramatically reduces the perceived risk.



**2. Mitigating Factors:**

*   **Stable Employment:** The five-year employment history is a key mitigating factor.  Consistent income provides a reliable stream of funds for debt repayment.
*   **No Prior Defaults:**  The complete absence of prior defaults significantly strengthens the applicant's profile. It suggests a disciplined approach to credit management.
*   **Reasonable Income:** While moderate, $72,000 provides a foundation for repayment, particularly when combined with the stability of employment.



**3. Overall Risk Rating:**

Medium

RISK_RATING: medium

---

**Disclaimer:** *This risk assessment is based solely on the limited data provided. A full credit analysis would require a more comprehensive review of the applicant’s financial history, including credit reports, bank statements, and verification of income and employment. This report is for internal use only and should not be distributed to the applicant.* 

Do you want me to:

*   Adjust the risk rating based on different assumptions (e.g., different loan amounts)?
*   Add more detailed risk scoring calculations?
```

```spl
-- Recipe 49: Regulatory News Monitor
-- Demonstrates: WHILE loops, CREATE FUNCTION (persona injection), iterative logging
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/49_regulatory_news_audit/audit_news.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/49_regulatory_news_audit/tools.py \
--       news_batch_path=cookbook/49_regulatory_news_audit/data/news_feed.txt

-- Compliance persona + audit instruction combined in one function.
-- (regulatory_auditor() persona is inlined here so GENERATE receives it
--  as a rendered template argument — avoids non-builtin function call in expressions.)
CREATE FUNCTION audit_news(news TEXT)
RETURN TEXT
AS $$
You are a senior compliance officer at a G-SIB.
Identify regulatory risks in the financial news item below.

Focus on: Sanctions, AML, Market Manipulation, AI Ethics.

Output STRICTLY valid JSON:
{ "risk_level": "low|medium|high", "flags": ["list"], "summary": "one sentence" }

News item:
{news}
$$;

WORKFLOW news_sentiment_monitor
INPUT:
  @news_batch_path TEXT DEFAULT 'cookbook/49_regulatory_news_audit/data/news_feed.txt',
  @log_dir TEXT DEFAULT 'cookbook/49_regulatory_news_audit/logs-spl'
OUTPUT: @compliance_report TEXT
DO
  LOGGING f'Starting compliance feed from "{@news_batch_path}" ...' LEVEL INFO

  CALL read_news_feed(@news_batch_path) INTO @news_batch
  CALL get_list_length(@news_batch) INTO @batch_size
  LOGGING f'News batch loaded with {@batch_size} items.' LEVEL INFO

  EVALUATE @batch_size
  WHEN = 0 THEN
    LOGGING f'No news data found at: {@news_batch_path}' LEVEL ERROR
    RETURN 'No data' WITH reason = 'feed_empty'
  END

  @batch_id := 0
  WHILE @batch_id < @batch_size DO
    LOGGING f'Processing batch {@batch_id}...' LEVEL INFO
    CALL get_item(@news_batch, @batch_id) INTO @news
    LOGGING f'News item:\n{@news}' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Audit the news item (LLM call)
    GENERATE audit_news(@news) INTO @audit_result

    -- Persist raw audit output
    CALL write_file(f'{@log_dir}/batch_{@batch_id}.json', @audit_result) INTO NONE

    -- Extract risk level deterministically
    CALL extract_json_field(@audit_result, 'risk_level') INTO @current_risk

    EVALUATE @current_risk
    WHEN 'high' THEN
      LOGGING f'CRITICAL ALERT in batch {@batch_id}!' LEVEL ERROR
      CALL send_alert(@audit_result) INTO NONE
    ELSE
      LOGGING f'Batch {@batch_id} clear ({@current_risk})' LEVEL INFO
    END

    @batch_id := @batch_id + 1
  END

  COMMIT 'Scan Complete' WITH total_batches = @batch_id
END
```
